<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">DECEMBER 31, 2017 AND 2016</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(1)&#160; Organization &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">AEI Income &amp; Growth Fund 25 LLC ("Company"), a Limited Liability Company, was formed on June&#160;24, 2002 to acquire and lease commercial properties to operating tenants.&#160; The Company's operations are managed by AEI Fund Management XXI, Inc. ("AFM"), the Managing Member.&#160; Robert P. Johnson, the President and sole director of AFM, serves as the Special Managing Member.&#160; AFM is a wholly owned subsidiary of AEI Capital Corporation of which Mr. Johnson is the majority shareholder.&#160; AEI Fund Management, Inc. ("AEI"), an affiliate of AFM, performs the administrative and operating functions for the Company.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The terms of the offering called for a subscription price of $1,000 per LLC Unit, payable on acceptance of the offer.&#160; The Company commenced operations on September&#160;11, 2003 when minimum subscriptions of 1,500 LLC Units ($1,500,000) were accepted.&#160; The offering terminated May&#160;12, 2005, when the extended offering period expired.&#160; The Company received subscriptions for 42,434.763 Units.&#160; Under the terms of the Operating Agreement, the Limited Members and Managing Members contributed funds of $42,434,763 and $1,000, respectively.&#160; The Company shall continue until December&#160;31, 2053, unless dissolved, terminated and liquidated prior to that date.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">During operations, any Net Cash Flow, as defined, which the Managing Members determine to distribute will be distributed 97% to the Limited Members and 3% to the Managing Members.&#160; Distributions to Limited Members will be made pro rata by Units.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Any Net Proceeds of Sale, as defined, from the sale or financing of properties which the Managing Members determine to distribute will, after provisions for debts and reserves, be paid in the following manner: (i) first, 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members until the Limited Members receive an amount equal to: (a) their Adjusted Capital Contribution plus (b) an amount equal to 7% of their Adjusted Capital Contribution per annum, cumulative but not compounded, to the extent not previously distributed from Net Cash Flow; (ii) any remaining balance will be distributed 90% to the Limited Members and 10% to the Managing Members.&#160; Distributions to the Limited Members will be made pro rata by Units.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For tax purposes, profits from operations, other than profits attributable to the sale, exchange, financing, refinancing or other disposition of property, will be allocated 97% to the Limited Members and 3% to the Managing Members.&#160; Net losses from operations will be allocated 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For tax purposes, profits arising from the sale, financing, or other disposition of property will be allocated in accordance with the Operating Agreement as follows: (i) first, to those Members with deficit balances in their capital accounts in an amount equal to the sum of such deficit balances; (ii) second, 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members until the aggregate balance in the Limited Members' capital accounts equals the sum of the Limited Members' Adjusted Capital Contributions plus an amount equal to 7% of their Adjusted Capital Contributions per annum, cumulative but not compounded, to the extent not previously allocated; (iii) third, the balance of any remaining gain will then be allocated 90% to the Limited Members and 10% to the Managing Members.&#160; Losses will be allocated 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Managing Members are not required to currently fund a deficit capital balance.&#160; Upon liquidation of the Company or withdrawal by a Managing Member, the Managing Members will contribute to the Company an amount equal to the lesser of the deficit balances in their capital accounts or 1.01% of the total capital contributions of the Limited Members over the amount previously contributed by the Managing Members.</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreakArea" style="MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-TOP: 10pt; CLEAR: both">
<div id="DSPFPageNumberArea" style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font id="DSPFPageNumber" style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: normal; FONT-STYLE: normal">-34-</font></div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<hr style="BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; HEIGHT: 2px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px; WIDTH: 100%; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; COLOR: #000000; CLEAR: both; MARGIN: 4px 0px; BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #000000" noshade="noshade">
</div>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">DECEMBER 31, 2017 AND 2016</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Financial Statement Presentation</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The accounts of the Company are maintained on the accrual basis of accounting for both federal income tax purposes and financial reporting purposes.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Accounting Estimates</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Management uses estimates and assumptions in preparing these financial statements in accordance with United States Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (US GAAP).&#160; Those estimates and assumptions may affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities, the disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities, and the reported revenues and expenses.&#160; Actual results could differ from those estimates.&#160; Significant items, subject to such estimates and assumptions, include the carrying value of real estate held for investment, real estate held for sale and related intangible assets.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company regularly assesses whether market events and conditions indicate that it is reasonably possible to recover the carrying amounts of its investments in real estate from future operations and sales.&#160; A change in those market events and conditions could have a material effect on the carrying amount of its real estate.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Cash Concentrations of Credit Risk</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company's cash is deposited in one financial institution and at times during the year it may exceed FDIC insurance limits.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Receivables</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Credit terms are extended to tenants in the normal course of business.&#160; The Company performs ongoing credit evaluations of its customers' financial condition and, generally, requires no collateral.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Receivables are recorded at their estimated net realizable value.&#160; The Company follows a policy of providing an allowance for doubtful accounts; however, based on historical experience, and its evaluation of the current status of receivables, the Company is of the belief that such accounts, if any, will be collectible in all material respects and thus an allowance is not necessary.&#160; Accounts are considered past due if payment is not made on a timely basis in accordance with the Company's credit terms.&#160; Receivables considered uncollectible are written off.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Income Taxes</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The income or loss of the Company for federal income tax reporting purposes is includable in the income tax returns of the Members.&#160; In general, no recognition has been given to income taxes in the accompanying financial statements.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The tax return and the amount of distributable Company income or loss are subject to examination by federal and state taxing authorities.&#160; If such an examination results in changes to distributable Company income or loss, the taxable income of the members would be adjusted accordingly.&#160; Primarily due to its tax status as a partnership, the Company has no significant tax uncertainties that require recognition or disclosure.&#160; The Company is no longer subject to U.S. federal income tax examinations for tax years before 2014, and with few exceptions, is no longer subject to state tax examinations for tax years before 2014.</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreakArea" style="MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-TOP: 10pt; CLEAR: both">
<div id="DSPFPageNumberArea" style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font id="DSPFPageNumber" style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: normal; FONT-STYLE: normal">-35-</font></div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<hr style="BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; HEIGHT: 2px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px; WIDTH: 100%; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; COLOR: #000000; CLEAR: both; MARGIN: 4px 0px; BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #000000" noshade="noshade">
</div>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">DECEMBER 31, 2017 AND 2016</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Revenue Recognition</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company's real estate is leased under net leases, classified as operating leases.&#160; The leases provide for base annual rental payments payable in monthly installments.&#160; The Company recognizes rental income according to the terms of the individual leases.&#160; For leases that contain stated rental increases, the increases are recognized in the year in which they are effective.&#160; Contingent rental payments are recognized when the contingencies on which the payments are based are satisfied and the rental payments become due under the terms of the leases.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Real Estate</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Upon acquisition of real properties, the Company records them in the financial statements at cost.&#160; The purchase price is allocated to tangible assets, consisting of land and building, and to identified intangible assets and liabilities, which may include the value of above market and below market leases and the value of in-place leases.&#160; The allocation of the purchase price is based upon the fair value of each component of the property.&#160; Although independent appraisals may be used to assist in the determination of fair value, in many cases these values will be based upon management's assessment of each property, the selling prices of comparable properties and the discounted value of cash flows from the asset.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The fair values of above market and below market in-place leases will be recorded based on the present value (using an interest rate which reflects the risks associated with the leases acquired) of the difference between (i)&#160;the contractual amounts to be paid pursuant to the in-place leases and (ii)&#160;an estimate of fair market lease rates for the corresponding in-place leases measured over a period equal to the non-cancelable term of the lease including any bargain renewal periods.&#160; The above market and below market lease values will be capitalized as intangible lease assets or liabilities.&#160; Above market lease values will be amortized as an adjustment of rental income over the remaining term of the respective leases.&#160; Below market lease values will be amortized as an adjustment of rental income over the remaining term of the respective leases, including any bargain renewal periods.&#160; If a lease were to be terminated prior to its stated expiration, all unamortized amounts of above market and below market in-place lease values relating to that lease would be recorded as an adjustment to rental income.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The fair values of in-place leases will include estimated direct costs associated with obtaining a new tenant, and opportunity costs associated with lost rentals which are avoided by acquiring an in-place lease.&#160; Direct costs associated with obtaining a new tenant may include commissions, tenant improvements, and other direct costs and are estimated, in part, by management's consideration of current market costs to execute a similar lease.&#160; These direct costs will be included in intangible lease assets on the balance sheet and will be amortized to expense over the remaining term of the respective leases.&#160; The value of opportunity costs will be calculated using the contractual amounts to be paid pursuant to the in-place leases over a market absorption period for a similar lease.&#160; These intangibles will be included in intangible lease assets on the balance sheet and will be amortized to expense over the remaining term of the respective leases.&#160; If a lease were to be terminated prior to its stated expiration, all unamortized amounts of in-place lease assets relating to that lease would be expensed.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreakArea" style="MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-TOP: 10pt; CLEAR: both">
<div id="DSPFPageNumberArea" style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font id="DSPFPageNumber" style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: normal; FONT-STYLE: normal">-36-</font></div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">

</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">DECEMBER 31, 2017 AND 2016</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company tests real estate for recoverability when events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying value may not be recoverable.&#160; For properties the Company will hold and operate, it compares the carrying amount of the property to the estimated probability-weighted future undiscounted cash flows expected to result from the property and its eventual disposition.&#160; If the sum of the expected future cash flows is less than the carrying amount of the property, the Company recognizes an impairment loss by the amount by which the carrying amount of the property exceeds the fair value of the property.&#160; For properties held for sale, the Company determines whether impairment has occurred by comparing the property's estimated fair value less cost to sell to its current carrying value.&#160; If the carrying value is greater than the net realizable value, an impairment loss is recorded to reduce the carrying value of the property to its net realizable value.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For financial reporting purposes, the buildings owned by the Company are depreciated using the straight-line method over an estimated useful life of 25 years.&#160; Intangible lease assets are amortized using the straight-line method for financial reporting purposes based on the remaining life of the lease.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The disposition of a property or classification of a property as Real Estate Held for Sale by the Company does not represent a strategic shift that will have a major effect on the Company's operations and financial results.&#160; Therefore, the results from operating and selling the property are included in continuing operations.&#160; However, if a property was classified as Real Estate Held for Sale at December 31, 2013, the property was considered discontinued operations under prior accounting guidance.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company accounts for properties owned as tenants-in-common with affiliated entities and/or unrelated third parties using the proportionate consolidation method.&#160; Each tenant-in-common owns a separate, undivided interest in the properties.&#160; Any tenant-in-common that holds more than a 50% interest does not control decisions over the other tenant-in-common interests.&#160; The financial statements reflect only this Company's percentage share of the properties' land, building, liabilities, revenues and expenses.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company's properties are subject to environmental laws and regulations adopted by various governmental entities in the jurisdiction in which the properties are located.&#160; These laws could require the Company to investigate and remediate the effects of the release or disposal of hazardous materials at these locations if found.&#160; For each property, an environmental assessment is completed prior to acquisition.&#160; In addition, the lease agreements typically strictly prohibit the production, handling, or storage of hazardous materials (except where incidental to the tenant's business such as use of cleaning supplies) in violation of applicable law to restrict environmental and other damage.&#160; Environmental liabilities are recorded when it is determined the liability is probable and the costs can reasonably be estimated.&#160; There were no environmental issues noted or liabilities recorded at December&#160;31, 2017 and 2016.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Fair Value Measurements</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">As of December&#160;31, 2017 and 2016, the Company had no assets or liabilities measured at fair value on a recurring basis or nonrecurring basis.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Income Per Unit</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Income per LLC Unit is calculated based on the weighted average number of LLC Units outstanding during each period presented.&#160; Diluted income per LLC Unit considers the effect of any potentially dilutive Unit equivalents, of which the Company had none for each of the years ended December&#160;31, 2017 and 2016.</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Summary of Significant Accounting Policies &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Reportable Segments</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company invests in single tenant commercial properties throughout the United States that are net leased to tenants in various industries.&#160; Because these net leased properties have similar economic characteristics, the Company evaluates operating performance on an overall portfolio basis.&#160; Therefore, the Company's properties are classified as one reportable segment.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In May 2014, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) 2014-09 regarding ASC Topic 606, Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#160; The standard provides principles for recognizing revenue for the transfer of promised goods or services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods or services.&#160; The guidance is effective for the Company's fiscal year beginning January&#160;1, 2018.&#160; We evaluated the accounting, transition, and disclosure requirements of the standard and the adoption of this standard will not have a material impact on the financial statements as the Company earns substantially all of its revenue from lease contracts that fall within the scope of AIC Topic 840, which are not within the scope of the new revenue standard.&#160; Additionally, we have historically disposed of properties for cash with no contingencies and no future investment in the properties.&#160; Therefore, the new revenue standard will not impact the recognition of gain or loss from property sales.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In February 2016, the FASB issued ASU 2016-02, which provides guidance for accounting for leases.&#160; The new guidance requires companies to recognize the assets and liabilities for the rights and obligations created by leased assets, initially measured at the present value of the lease payments.&#160; The accounting guidance for lessors is largely unchanged.&#160; The ASU is effective for annual and interim periods beginning after December&#160;15, 2018 with early adoption permitted.&#160; It is to be adopted using a modified retrospective approach.&#160; Management is currently evaluating the impact the adoption of this guidance will have on the Company's financial statements.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In January 2017, the FASB issued ASU 2017-01, which clarifies the definition of a business by adding guidance to assist entities in evaluating whether transactions should be accounted for as acquisitions (or disposals) of assets or businesses.&#160; The guidance is effective for annual periods beginning after December&#160;15, 2017, including interim periods within those periods, with early adoption permitted, and is required to be applied prospectively to any transactions occurring within the period of adoption.&#160; We are currently evaluating the accounting and disclosure requirements of the standard.&#160; We expect the new standard will result in the majority of our real estate acquisitions to be considered asset acquisitions, whereby external acquisition costs related to these asset acquisitions will be capitalized.&#160; Currently, the majority of our real estate acquisitions are considered acquisitions of businesses, whereby all acquisition-related costs are expensed as incurred.&#160; We do not expect the standard to have a significant impact on the allocation of purchase price to tangible and identifiable intangible assets and liabilities acquired based on their respective fair values.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(4)&#160; Real Estate Investments &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company leases its properties to tenants under net leases, classified as operating leases.&#160; Under a net lease, the tenant is responsible for real estate taxes, insurance, maintenance, repairs and operating expenses for the property.&#160; For some leases, the Company is responsible for repairs to the structural components of the building, the roof, and the parking lot.&#160; At the time the properties were acquired, the remaining primary lease terms varied from 10 to 20 years, except for the Staples store, which had a remaining primary term of 8.4 years, and the Premier Diagnostic Imaging center, which had a remaining primary term of 7.8 years.&#160; The lease for the Advance Auto Parts store was extended to expire on April 30, 2025.&#160; The leases provide the tenants with one to five five-year renewal options subject to the same terms and conditions as the primary term.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company's properties are commercial, single-tenant buildings.&#160; The Jared Jewelry store in Madison Heights, Michigan was constructed in 2003 and acquired in 2004.&#160; The Jared Jewelry store in Auburn Hills, Michigan was constructed in 1999 and acquired in 2005.&#160; The Tractor Supply Company store was constructed in 2003 and acquired in 2005.&#160; The Jared Jewelry store in Concord, New Hampshire was constructed and acquired in 2005.&#160; The Jared Jewelry store in Aurora, Illinois was constructed in 2000 and acquired in 2005.&#160; The building in Wichita, Kansas was constructed in 1996, renovated in 2001 and acquired in 2005.&#160; The Advance Auto Parts store in Indianapolis, Indiana was constructed in 2005 and acquired in 2006.&#160; The land for the Dick's Sporting Goods store was acquired in 2007 and construction of the store was completed in 2008.&#160; The Staples store was constructed in 2010 and acquired in 2011.&#160; The Coliseum Health clinic was constructed and acquired in 2012.&#160; The PetSmart store was constructed and acquired in 2013.&#160; The Premier Diagnostic Imaging center was constructed in 2005, renovated in 2012 and acquired in 2014.&#160; There have been no costs capitalized as improvements subsequent to the acquisitions, except for $7,733 of tenant improvements related to the Staples store.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">DECEMBER 31, 2017 AND 2016</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(4)&#160; Real Estate Investments &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company owns a 60% interest in the Sports Authority store in Wichita, Kansas.&#160; On March&#160;2, 2016, the tenant, TSA Stores, Inc., and its parent company, The Sports Authority, Inc., the guarantor of the lease, filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy reorganization.&#160; In June 2016, the tenant filed a motion with the bankruptcy court to reject the lease for this store effective June&#160;30, 2016, at which time the tenant returned possession of the property to the owners.&#160;&#160; As of December&#160;31, 2017, the tenant owed $29,049 of past due rent, which was not accrued for financial reporting purposes.&#160; The owners listed the property for lease with a real estate broker in the Wichita area.&#160; While the property is vacant, the Company is responsible for its 60% share of real estate taxes and other costs associated with maintaining the property.&#160; The annual rent from this property represented approximately 13% of the total annual rent of the Company's property portfolio.&#160; The loss of rent and increased expenses related to this property decreased the Company's cash flow.&#160; Consequently, beginning with the third quarter of 2016, the Company reduced its regular quarterly cash distribution rate from $12.85 per Unit to $10.27&#160;per Unit.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">On September 21, 2017, the Company entered into a lease agreement with a primary term of 10&#160;years with Biomat USA, Inc. ("Biomat") as a replacement tenant for 28% of the square footage of the property.&#160; The tenant will operate a Biomat USA Plasma Center in the space.&#160; The Company's 60% share of annual rent is $55,607 and is expected to commence on June&#160;18, 2018.&#160; Biomat has agreed to pay for the costs to divide the building into two separate spaces, the costs of tenant improvements to remodel the Biomat space and 28% of the cost to replace the roof.&#160; The Company will be responsible for paying its 60% share of the remaining cost to replace the roof, which is expected to be approximately $170,000.&#160; At December 31, 2017, the Company accrued its 60% share of lease commissions due to real estate brokers totaling $81,440 that were owed as part of the lease transaction.&#160; This amount was capitalized and will be amortized over the term of the lease.&#160; The Company is continuing to pursue additional tenants for the remaining space.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In the third quarter of 2017, the Company decided to sell the Fresenius Medical Center in Gretna, Louisiana.&#160; In October&#160;2017, the Company entered into an agreement to sell the property to an unrelated third party.&#160; On December&#160;6, 2017, the sale closed with the Company receiving net proceeds of $3,939,360, which resulted in a net gain of $757,670.&#160; At the time of sale, the cost and related accumulated depreciation and amortization was $3,456,892 and $275,202, respectively.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In February 2018, the Company entered into an agreement with the tenant of the Advance Auto Parts store in Indianapolis, Indiana to extend the lease term five years to expire on April&#160;30, 2025.&#160; As part of the agreement, the annual rent decreased from $51,630 to $44,079 effective January&#160;1, 2018.&#160; In addition, beginning on March&#160;1, 2018, the tenant will receive free rent for four months that equals $14,693.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(6)&#160; Discontinued Operations &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The tenant of the Johnny Carino's restaurants was experiencing financial difficulties and closed the restaurants in Pueblo, Colorado (October 2013) and Lake Charles, Louisiana (January 2014). On March 27, 2014, the tenant filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy reorganization.&#160; Shortly thereafter, the tenant filed a motion with the bankruptcy court to reject the leases and returned possession of the properties to the Company.&#160; As of the date of the bankruptcy filing, the tenant owed $97,680 of past due rent, which was not accrued for financial reporting purposes.&#160; While the properties were vacant, the Company was responsible for the real estate taxes and other costs associated with maintaining the properties.&#160; The Company submitted a Proof of Claim for damages to the bankruptcy court for each property.&#160; The tenant's reorganization plan was approved by the bankruptcy court effective February 2, 2015.&#160; In August 2015, the Company received payments totaling $137,474 on its claims from the plan.&#160; In 2016, the Company received final claim payments totaling $27,258.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In September 2013, the Company decided to sell both Johnny Carino's restaurants and classified them as Real Estate Held for Sale. On August 1, 2014, the Company sold the Lake Charles property to an unrelated third party.&#160; In late March 2016, the Company entered into an agreement to sell the Pueblo property to an unrelated third party.&#160; On August 4, 2016, the sale closed with the Company receiving net proceeds of $749,867, which resulted in a net gain of $99,867.&#160; At the time of sale, the carrying value of the property was $650,000.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(7)&#160; Members' Capital &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For the years ended December&#160;31, 2017 and 2016, the Company declared distributions of $2,002,213 and $1,928,190, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members received distributions of $1,948,005 and $1,875,395 and the Managing Members received distributions of $54,208 and $52,795 for the years, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members' distributions represented $48.50 and $46.33 per LLC Unit outstanding using 40,163 and 40,482 weighted average Units in 2017 and 2016, respectively.&#160; The distributions represented $35.76 and $19.12 per Unit of Net Income and $12.74 and $27.21 per Unit of return of contributed capital in 2017 and 2016, respectively.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">As part of the distributions discussed above, the Company distributed net sale proceeds of $292,929 and $252,525 in 2017 and 2016, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members received distributions of $290,000 and $250,000 and the Managing Members received distributions of $2,929 and $2,525 for the years, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members' distributions represented $7.24 and $6.16 per Unit for the years, respectively.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company may repurchase Units from Limited Members who have tendered their Units to the Company.&#160; Such Units may be acquired at a discount.&#160; The Company will not be obligated to purchase in any year more than 2% of the total number of Units outstanding on January 1 of such year.&#160; In no event shall the Company be obligated to purchase Units if, in the sole discretion of the Managing Member, such purchase would impair the capital or operation of the Company.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">During 2017, the Company repurchased a total of 174.25 Units for $117,841 from 10 Limited Members in accordance with the Operating Agreement.&#160; On October&#160;1, 2016, the Company repurchased a total of 353.30 Units for $234,074 from 17 Limited Members. The Company acquired these Units using Net Cash Flow from operations.&#160; The repurchases increase the remaining Limited Members' ownership interest in the Company.&#160; As a result of these repurchases and pursuant to the Operating Agreement, the Managing Members received distributions of $3,644 and $7,239 in 2017 and 2016, respectively.</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<hr style="BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; HEIGHT: 2px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px; WIDTH: 100%; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; COLOR: #000000; CLEAR: both; MARGIN: 4px 0px; BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #000000" noshade="noshade">
</div>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">MARCH 31, 2018</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: center">(unaudited)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify"><font style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold">(1)</font>&#160; The condensed statements included herein have been prepared by the registrant, without audit, pursuant to the rules and regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission, and reflect all adjustments which are, in the opinion of management, necessary to a fair statement of the results of operations for the interim period, on a basis consistent with the annual audited statements.&#160; The adjustments made to these condensed statements consist only of normal recurring adjustments.&#160; Certain information, accounting policies, and footnote disclosures normally included in financial statements prepared in accordance with United States Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (US GAAP) have been condensed or omitted pursuant to such rules and regulations, although the registrant believes that the disclosures are adequate to make the information presented not misleading.&#160; It is suggested that these condensed financial statements be read in conjunction with the financial statements and the summary of significant accounting policies and notes thereto included in the registrant's latest annual report on Form&#160;10&#8209;K.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Organization &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">AEI Income &amp; Growth Fund 25 LLC ("Company"), a Limited Liability Company, was formed on June&#160;24, 2002 to acquire and lease commercial properties to operating tenants.&#160; The Company's operations are managed by AEI Fund Management XXI, Inc. ("AFM"), the Managing Member.&#160; Robert P. Johnson, the President and sole director of AFM, serves as the Special Managing Member.&#160; AFM is a wholly owned subsidiary of AEI Capital Corporation of which Mr. Johnson is the majority shareholder.&#160; AEI Fund Management, Inc. ("AEI"), an affiliate of AFM, performs the administrative and operating functions for the Company.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The terms of the offering called for a subscription price of $1,000 per LLC Unit, payable on acceptance of the offer.&#160; The Company commenced operations on September&#160;11, 2003 when minimum subscriptions of 1,500 LLC Units ($1,500,000) were accepted.&#160; The offering terminated May&#160;12, 2005, when the extended offering period expired.&#160; The Company received subscriptions for 42,434.763 Units.&#160; Under the terms of the Operating Agreement, the Limited Members and Managing Members contributed funds of $42,434,763 and $1,000, respectively.&#160; The Company shall continue until December&#160;31, 2053, unless dissolved, terminated and liquidated prior to that date.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">During operations, any Net Cash Flow, as defined, which the Managing Members determine to distribute will be distributed 97% to the Limited Members and 3% to the Managing Members.&#160; Distributions to Limited Members will be made pro rata by Units.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Any Net Proceeds of Sale, as defined, from the sale or financing of properties which the Managing Members determine to distribute will, after provisions for debts and reserves, be paid in the following manner: (i) first, 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members until the Limited Members receive an amount equal to: (a) their Adjusted Capital Contribution plus (b) an amount equal to 7% of their Adjusted Capital Contribution per annum, cumulative but not compounded, to the extent not previously distributed from Net Cash Flow; (ii) any remaining balance will be distributed 90% to the Limited Members and 10% to the Managing Members.&#160; Distributions to the Limited Members will be made pro rata by Units.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For tax purposes, profits from operations, other than profits attributable to the sale, exchange, financing, refinancing or other disposition of property, will be allocated 97% to the Limited Members and 3% to the Managing Members.&#160; Net losses from operations will be allocated 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreakArea" style="MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-TOP: 10pt; CLEAR: both">
<div id="DSPFPageNumberArea" style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font id="DSPFPageNumber" style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: normal; FONT-STYLE: normal">-50-</font></div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<hr style="BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; HEIGHT: 2px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px; WIDTH: 100%; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; COLOR: #000000; CLEAR: both; MARGIN: 4px 0px; BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #000000" noshade="noshade">
</div>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">(Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(2)&#160; Organization &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For tax purposes, profits arising from the sale, financing, or other disposition of property will be allocated in accordance with the Operating Agreement as follows: (i) first, to those Members with deficit balances in their capital accounts in an amount equal to the sum of such deficit balances; (ii) second, 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members until the aggregate balance in the Limited Members' capital accounts equals the sum of the Limited Members' Adjusted Capital Contributions plus an amount equal to 7% of their Adjusted Capital Contributions per annum, cumulative but not compounded, to the extent not previously allocated; (iii) third, the balance of any remaining gain will then be allocated 90% to the Limited Members and 10% to the Managing Members.&#160; Losses will be allocated 99% to the Limited Members and 1% to the Managing Members.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Managing Members are not required to currently fund a deficit capital balance.&#160; Upon liquidation of the Company or withdrawal by a Managing Member, the Managing Members will contribute to the Company an amount equal to the lesser of the deficit balances in their capital accounts or 1.01% of the total capital contributions of the Limited Members over the amount previously contributed by the Managing Members.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(3)&#160; Recently Adopted Accounting Pronouncements &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In May 2014, with subsequent updates issued in August 2015 and March, April and May 2016, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB) issued Accounting Standards Update (ASU) No. 2014-09 regarding ASC Topic 606, Revenue from Contracts with Customers.&#160; This standard was developed to enable financial statement users to better understand the nature, amount, timing and uncertainty of revenue and cash flows arising from contracts with customers.&#160; The update's core principle is that an entity should recognize revenue to depict the transfer of promised goods or services to customers in an amount that reflects the consideration to which the entity expects to be entitled in exchange for those goods or services.&#160; Entities are to use a five-step contract review model to ensure revenue is recognized, measured and disclosed in accordance with this principle.&#160; Those steps include the following:&#160; (i) identify the contract with the customer, (ii) identify the performance obligations in the contract, (iii) determine the transaction price, (iv) allocate the transaction price to each performance obligation in the contract, and (v) recognize revenue when or as the entity satisfies a performance obligation.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">Management has concluded that all of the Company's material revenue streams fall outside of the scope of this guidance.&#160; The new standard may be applied retrospectively to each prior period presented or prospectively with the cumulative effect, if any, recognized as of the date of adoption.&#160; During 2018, the Company selected the modified retrospective transition method as of the date of adoption effective January&#160;1, 2018.&#160; Management has concluded that the majority of total revenues consist of rental income from leasing arrangements, which are specifically excluded from the standard.&#160; The Company analyzed its remaining revenue streams, inclusive of gains and losses on real estate sales, and concluded there are no changes in revenue recognition with the adoption of the new standard.&#160; As such, adoption of the standard did not result in a cumulative adjustment recognized as of January&#160;1, 2018, and the standard did not have a material impact on the Company's financial statements.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreakArea" style="MARGIN-BOTTOM: 10pt; MARGIN-TOP: 10pt; CLEAR: both">
<div id="DSPFPageNumberArea" style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font id="DSPFPageNumber" style="FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: normal; FONT-STYLE: normal">-51-</font></div>

<div id="DSPFPageBreak" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
<hr style="BORDER-LEFT-WIDTH: 0px; HEIGHT: 2px; BORDER-RIGHT-WIDTH: 0px; WIDTH: 100%; BORDER-BOTTOM-WIDTH: 0px; COLOR: #000000; CLEAR: both; MARGIN: 4px 0px; BORDER-TOP-WIDTH: 0px; BACKGROUND-COLOR: #000000" noshade="noshade">
</div>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">AEI INCOME &amp; GROWTH FUND 25 LLC</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">NOTES TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: center">(Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(3)&#160; Recently Adopted Accounting Pronouncements &#8211; (Continued)</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In January 2017, the FASB issued ASU 2017-01, which clarifies the definition of a business by adding guidance to assist entities in evaluating whether transactions should be accounted for as acquisitions (or disposals) of assets or businesses.&#160; The guidance is effective for annual periods beginning after December&#160;15, 2017, including interim periods within those periods, with early adoption permitted, and is required to be applied prospectively to any transactions occurring within the period of adoption.&#160; We expect the new standard will result in all of our real estate acquisitions being considered asset acquisitions, whereby substantially all acquisition costs related to our real estate acquisitions will be capitalized.&#160; Prior to the adoption of the new standard, all of our real estate acquisitions completed after January&#160;1, 2009, were considered acquisitions of businesses, whereby all acquisition-related costs were expensed as incurred.&#160; During 2018, the Company has adopted the accounting pronouncement effective January&#160;1, 2018, and applied this guidance prospectively.&#160; The adoption did not have a material effect on its financial statements.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">(4)&#160; Real Estate Investments &#8211;</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">The Company owns a 60% interest in the Sports Authority store in Wichita, Kansas.&#160; On March&#160;2, 2016, the tenant, TSA Stores, Inc., and its parent company, The Sports Authority, Inc., the guarantor of the lease, filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy reorganization.&#160; In June 2016, the tenant filed a motion with the bankruptcy court to reject the lease for this store effective June&#160;30, 2016, at which time the tenant returned possession of the property to the owners.&#160;&#160; As of March&#160;31, 2018, the tenant owed $29,049 of past due rent, which was not accrued for financial reporting purposes.&#160; The owners listed the property for lease with a real estate broker in the Wichita area.&#160; While the property is vacant, the Company is responsible for its 60% share of real estate taxes and other costs associated with maintaining the property.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">On September 21, 2017, the Company entered into a lease agreement with a primary term of 10&#160;years with Biomat USA, Inc. ("Biomat") as a replacement tenant for 28% of the square footage of the property.&#160; The tenant will operate a Biomat USA Plasma Center in the space.&#160; The Company's 60% share of annual rent is $55,607 and is expected to commence on June&#160;18, 2018.&#160; Biomat has agreed to pay for the costs to divide the building into two separate spaces, the costs of tenant improvements to remodel the Biomat space and 28% of the cost to replace the roof.&#160; The Company will be responsible for paying its 60% share of the remaining cost to replace the roof, which is expected to be approximately $170,000.&#160; At December 31, 2017, the Company accrued its 60% share of lease commissions due to real estate brokers totaling $81,440 that were owed as part of the lease transaction.&#160; This amount was capitalized and will be amortized over the term of the lease.&#160; The Company is continuing to pursue additional tenants for the remaining space.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In the third quarter of 2017, the Company decided to sell the Fresenius Medical Center in Gretna, Louisiana.&#160; In October&#160;2017, the Company entered into an agreement to sell the property to an unrelated third party.&#160; On December&#160;6, 2017, the sale closed with the Company receiving net proceeds of $3,939,360, which resulted in a net gain of $757,670.&#160; At the time of sale, the cost and related accumulated depreciation and amortization was $3,456,892 and $275,202, respectively.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">In February 2018, the Company entered into an agreement with the tenant of the Advance Auto Parts store in Indianapolis, Indiana to extend the lease term five years to end on April&#160;30, 2025.&#160; As part of the agreement, the annual rent decreased from $51,630 to $44,079 effective January&#160;1, 2018.&#160; In addition, beginning on March&#160;1, 2018, the tenant will receive free rent for four months that equals $14,693.</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">AEI Fund Management, Inc. performs the administrative and operating functions for the Company.&#160; The payable to AEI Fund Management represents the balance due for those services.&#160; This balance is non-interest bearing and unsecured and is to be paid in the normal course of business.</div>

<div style="FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: 'Times New Roman', Times, serif; TEXT-ALIGN: justify">For the three months ended March&#160;31, 2018 and 2017, the Company declared distributions of $424,330 and $427,322, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members received distributions of $411,600 and $414,503 and the Managing Members received distributions of $12,730 and $12,819 for the periods, respectively.&#160; The Limited Members' distributions represented $10.28 and $10.31 per LLC Unit outstanding using 40,042 and 40,217 weighted average Units in 2018 and 2017, respectively.&#160; The distributions represented $4.80 and $4.97 per Unit of Net Income and $5.48 and $5.34 per Unit of return of contributed capital in 2018 and 2017, respectively.</div>
